Implement Phase 1 only: Business + Membership Foundation.

Bliq is both:
- a web app
- an iOS app
- an Android app

Use a shared Next.js codebase for web and mobile-wrapped app flows. Even though this phase is backend-heavy, build all route/service/API decisions in a way that supports both web and mobile clients cleanly.

Do not move to Phase 2 until Phase 1 builds successfully.

PHASE 1 GOAL:
Create the tenant ownership and access-control foundation for Bliq.

Before Bliq can support bookings, staff, services, storefronts, payments, AI, messaging, or mobile dashboards, it must know:
- who the user is
- which businesses they belong to
- what role they have in each business
- whether they are allowed to access or mutate business-owned data

Build only the following:

1. Prisma Client

Create or verify:

src/lib/prisma.ts

Requirements:
- export a shared `prisma` client
- use singleton PrismaClient pattern
- safe for Next.js hot reload
- no duplicate Prisma clients in development
- no direct Prisma client creation scattered across services

2. Event Logger

Create or verify:

src/lib/events.ts

Implement:

logEvent({
  type,
  source,
  level?,
  businessId?,
  actorUserId?,
  subjectType?,
  subjectId?,
  payload?
})

Requirements:
- write to the Event table
- default level to INFO
- never crash the main application flow if event logging fails
- catch logging errors internally
- console.error only when logging itself fails
- support web and mobile-triggered events equally
- event payload should be JSON-safe
- no secrets should ever be logged

Events to support in this phase:
- BUSINESS_CREATED
- BUSINESS_UPDATED
- BUSINESS_ACCESS_CHECKED
- BUSINESS_ACCESS_DENIED
- MEMBERSHIP_CREATED

3. Business Service

Create:

src/services/business/businessService.ts

Implement:

createBusiness({
  ownerUserId,
  name,
  slug,
  timezone?
})

getBusinessById({
  businessId
})

getBusinessBySlug({
  slug
})

updateBusiness({
  businessId,
  actorUserId,
  data
})

Requirements:
- create Business and OWNER BusinessMembership in one Prisma transaction
- slug must be unique
- validate required fields
- normalize slug where sensible
- emit BUSINESS_CREATED when a business is created
- emit MEMBERSHIP_CREATED when owner membership is created
- emit BUSINESS_UPDATED when a business is updated
- no HTTP/request/response logic in this file
- do not build UI in this phase
- do not build mobile screens in this phase
- keep the service reusable by web routes and future mobile API clients

4. Membership Service

Create:

src/services/business/membershipService.ts

Implement:

getUserBusinesses({
  userId
})

assertUserCanAccessBusiness({
  userId,
  businessId
})

assertUserRole({
  userId,
  businessId,
  allowedRoles
})

Requirements:
- use BusinessMembership table
- enforce business-scoped access
- throw clear errors for unauthorized access
- emit BUSINESS_ACCESS_CHECKED when access succeeds where appropriate
- emit BUSINESS_ACCESS_DENIED when access fails where appropriate
- do not return cross-tenant data
- do not assume one user can only ever have one business
- support future mobile app session usage
- support future staff/backup-admin roles cleanly

5. Thin API Routes

Create:

POST /api/businesses
GET /api/businesses
GET /api/businesses/[businessId]
PATCH /api/businesses/[businessId]

Requirements:
- use Next.js App Router route handlers
- use Zod validation
- route handlers must stay thin
- route handlers should parse request, call services, return JSON
- no business logic inside route handlers
- no direct Prisma queries in route handlers unless absolutely necessary
- for now, accept temporary userId/actorUserId in request body/query until real auth is implemented
- clearly mark this with TODO comments:
  "TODO: Replace temporary userId with authenticated session context in Auth phase."
- return consistent JSON responses for both web and mobile clients

Suggested response shape:

Success:
{
  "ok": true,
  "data": ...
}

Failure:
{
  "ok": false,
  "error": {
    "code": "ERROR_CODE",
    "message": "Human readable message"
  }
}

6. Mobile/Web API Compatibility

Because Bliq will be used from:
- browser web app
- iOS wrapper
- Android wrapper

Ensure:
- API responses are JSON-clean
- errors are predictable
- no server response depends on desktop-only assumptions
- business APIs can be called from mobile screens later
- route outputs are consistent enough for React hooks/mobile UI to consume

7. Do NOT build yet

Do not build:
- auth provider integration
- staff
- services/catalog
- availability
- bookings
- payments
- storefronts
- messaging
- AI modules
- mobile UI screens
- dashboard UI

This phase is strictly the foundation for business ownership and access control.

8. Quality Requirements

After implementation:
- run TypeScript check if available
- run build if possible
- fix all import/type errors
- ensure no broken routes
- summarize changed files
- explain how to test every API route
- explain any assumptions made
- list any TODOs left for the Auth phase

Remember:
- Bliq is a serious multi-tenant platform.
- Web and mobile clients must both be supported.
- Mobile is likely the primary user experience.
- Build clean foundations now so mobile and web can share the same backend safely.

Pick your default onboarding persona for the first 90 days:

Owner-operator (also works clients) vs owner-manager (mostly schedules others).

which one?

Go owner-operator for the first 90 days. No debate.

Here’s the reasoning, straight and practical:

Why owner-operator wins (early stage)
You’re building Bliq, not just testing a UI—you’re validating:

booking flows

real-world scheduling edge cases

customer behaviour (no-shows, late arrivals, preferences)

pricing sensitivity

messaging patterns (how people actually book)

friction points in mobile usage

You cannot simulate this properly as an owner-manager.

What owner-operator gives you that you cannot fake
1. Ground truth data (your biggest asset)
You’ll see:

“people always ask for X time”

“people don’t understand Y step”

“this UI is annoying on mobile”

“customers don’t care about feature Z at all”

That feeds directly into:

product decisions

AI logic later

automation rules

pricing strategy

2. Real operational pain (this is gold)
You’ll feel:

double bookings stress

last-minute cancellations

scheduling inefficiencies

communication gaps

Those pains become:

Bliq features that actually matter

Not guesswork.

3. Faster product iteration loop
You become:

user → tester → builder → deployer

Same day loop:

notice issue

tweak in Cursor

test next day

That’s insane velocity.

4. Stronger product intuition
After ~60 days you’ll instinctively know:

what matters

what’s noise

what’s scalable

what’s niche

That’s how real platforms are built.

Why NOT owner-manager (yet)
If you go straight to managing others:

You’ll be:

guessing workflows

relying on second-hand feedback

missing micro-frictions

building features nobody truly needs

That’s how products become:

bloated, complex, and useless

The hybrid (what you actually do)
You’re not just “a barber” or “a service provider”

You’re:

Operator + Product Architect

So your setup should be:

Weeks 1–4
100% owner-operator

run real bookings

use Bliq manually where possible

Weeks 5–8
still operating

start introducing 1–2 additional staff (if possible)

test multi-user flows

Weeks 9–12
start shifting slightly toward manager

test delegation

test dashboard usefulness

unrealistic slot gaps

This is a strong Phase 2 output. Keep the tenant-nested API style.

Use:

/api/businesses/[businessId]/...
not flat routes like:

For Bliq, tenant-nested is cleaner because almost everything belongs to a business. It makes the API easier to reason about for web + mobile clients and reduces accidental cross-tenant mistakes.

i asked cursor whats its understanding of bliq and it said...


What it is
Bliq is framed as a mobile-first, AI-native operating platform for appointment-based service businesses—not “just a booking app” and not barber-only. Barbers might be an early wedge, but the domain model is deliberately generic: Business, Staff, Service, Customer, Booking, availability, payments, etc.

Who it’s for
Any business that runs on appointments and services: salons, tutors, trainers, tattoo artists, consultants, mechanics, mobile beauty, home services, and similar. The idea is one platform that can stretch across many verticals.

Where it’s going (vision)
The build plan states the long-term aim: help a service business run bookings, customers, payments, storefronts, messaging, automation, and intelligence from one system—i.e. an OS for the business, not a single-feature tool.

How the business shows up in the product today
Technically, everything tenant-owned is scoped under a business (businessId), with Stripe (and later other PSPs) behind abstractions, and APIs designed so a future native app (e.g. Capacitor) or any client can consume the same HTTP surface.

In one line
Bliq is positioning as the central platform for running an appointment-based service business end-to-end, with generic primitives and multi-tenant design from the start, even if the first go-to-market niche is narrow.

Bliq — Source of Truth
1. What Bliq Is
Bliq is a mobile-first, multi-tenant, AI-ready operating system for service businesses.

It is NOT:

just a booking app

just for barbers

a niche tool

It IS:

a platform that allows any service-based business to run its operations end-to-end

Core idea:

Bliq replaces fragmented tools (booking apps, spreadsheets, messaging, payments, admin) with a single unified system.

2. Core Product Vision
Bliq helps businesses manage:

bookings

customers

staff

services

availability

payments

storefronts

messaging

automation

AI-driven insights

Over time, Bliq becomes:

the central operating layer for how service businesses run.

3. Target Users
Bliq must support:

barbers

salons

nail techs

lash techs

tutors

personal trainers

tattoo artists

consultants

mechanics

mobile/home service providers

Rule:

Never design anything that only works for one niche.

Everything must be generic and extensible.

4. Platform Nature
Bliq is:

multi-tenant (everything scoped by businessId)

API-first (web + mobile consume same APIs)

mobile-first (most users will use mobile)

event-driven (important actions emit events)

service-layer driven (business logic lives in services)

AI-augmented (but AI is never the source of truth)

5. Architecture Rules (Non-Negotiable)
5.1 Service Layer
ALL business logic must live in src/services/*

NO business logic in API routes

NO business logic in UI components

5.2 API Design
Always use tenant-nested routes:

/api/businesses/[businessId]/...

Examples:

/api/businesses/[businessId]/staff

/api/businesses/[businessId]/services

/api/businesses/[businessId]/bookings

Never create:

/api/staff

/api/services

5.3 Multi-Tenancy
Every query MUST be scoped by businessId

No cross-tenant data access

No global queries unless explicitly required and documented

5.4 Data Integrity
Never hard delete important records:

staff

services

bookings

customers

Use:

active / inactive flags

5.5 Events
Every important action must emit events:

Examples:

BUSINESS_CREATED

STAFF_CREATED

SERVICE_UPDATED

BOOKING_CREATED

PAYMENT_SUCCEEDED

Rules:

Events must never crash main flow

Events must not contain sensitive data

5.6 Validation
All API input must use Zod

Services must validate critical logic even if API validates

Never trust frontend.

5.7 Mobile-First Requirement
All decisions must assume:

The primary user is on mobile.

Implications:

simple flows

minimal steps

clear feedback

no complex UI assumptions

no hover interactions

no desktop-only thinking

5.8 Web Compatibility
Everything must still work on web

Layouts must be responsive

APIs must be consistent across clients

6. Booking Philosophy
Booking logic must be:

deterministic

backend-controlled

conflict-safe

Rules:

No double booking

No booking outside availability

No booking inactive staff/service

No booking during time off

Slot engine is the source of truth.

7. Payment Philosophy
Payments must be abstracted

Stripe is first provider, not permanent dependency

Mulah may replace or extend payments later

Rules:

No Stripe logic inside booking services

No card data storage

All payments go through paymentService

8. Messaging Philosophy
Bliq must eventually support:

WhatsApp

SMS

Instagram

Snapchat identity

Rules:

Do not fake integrations

Build real webhook boundaries

Log all messages

Separate identity from customer until confirmed

9. Storefront Philosophy
Bliq is NOT just backend.

Businesses should have:

public-facing pages

brand presence

booking entry points

Rules:

template-driven (not drag-and-drop builder)

mobile-first design

integrates directly into booking

10. AI Philosophy
AI is:

assistive

observational

analytical

AI is NOT:

authoritative

allowed to override core logic

allowed to execute destructive actions automatically

Rules:

All AI calls go through shared AI client

All AI outputs are logged

AI never validates bookings, payments, or permissions

11. UX Philosophy
Bliq must feel:

fast

clean

modern

premium

simple

Avoid:

clutter

enterprise bloat

complex forms

unnecessary steps

# Bliq — where we are now (snapshot)

_Generated for product/engineering alignment; update as releases ship._

## Business / product

**What Bliq is:** A **mobile-first, multi-tenant operating system** for appointment-based service businesses — generic **Business → Staff → Service → Customer → Booking** model (not a single-vertical app).

**What customers get (today):** Mostly **API-first** — there is a minimal marketing/home surface, but **no full consumer booking UI or public slug booking flow yet**. Bookings are created and managed through **authenticated-style tenant APIs** (temporary userId / actorUserId until real auth).

**What businesses get (today):** **Tenant-scoped operations** via HTTP: businesses and memberships, staff and service catalog (with who-can-perform-what), customers and channel identities, **bookings with staff overlap protection**, availability rules and time off, feature flags, **payment intent records + Stripe PaymentIntent when keys are set**, and **Payment rows on successful webhook**.

**Strategic gaps vs long-term vision:** Real **sessions (OAuth / Supabase / Clerk)**, **slot engine + public booking**, **notifications**, **messaging channels (WhatsApp, etc.)**, **storefront**, **Capacitor apps**, and **AI/ops tables** are planned in [TRANCHES.md](./TRANCHES.md) / master appendices — not shipped as product-complete UX yet.

## Infra / tech

| Area | State |
|------|--------|
| **Stack** | Next.js App Router, TypeScript, Tailwind, Prisma, PostgreSQL (Supabase-friendly URLs). |
| **Tenancy** | All tenant data under /api/businesses/[businessId]/...; membershipService on routes. |
| **Architecture** | Business logic in src/services/*; thin routes; Zod; logEvent for mutations. |
| **DB** | Prisma schema with core domain + payments + events; migrations in prisma/migrations/. |
| **Payments** | **Phase 7:** Stripe create + **POST /api/webhooks/stripe** + Payment on success. PSP code only under src/services/payments/*. |
| **CI** | GitHub Actions: install, prisma generate, lint, typecheck, build (dummy DATABASE_URL). |
| **Docs** | BLIQ_BUILD_PLAN (source of truth), ROADMAP, MASTER_SPINE + appendices, REPO_DELTA, FOLDER_STRUCTURE. |
| **Auth** | **Temporary** query/body user identity — replace in tranche T1. |

**Production checklist (short):** Configure real DATABASE_URL / DIRECT_URL, enable auth, add rate limits on public endpoints when they exist, configure Stripe webhook URL in Dashboard, secrets only in env / host manager.
